**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is April, 2025. The executive branch, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025] and tech czar Elon Musk [The Head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)], expands their power dramatically. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. 

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2

    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.

**Step 2 (logic-heavy)**

Put Articles into Categories: 

Cluster the hundreds of news articles into the these areas and topics you defined in Step 1. You must put **each** news article **uniquely** into one area and then one topic under area, and you can decide what the best choice is. Grab the news articles by their entire JSON lines for future reference. First, for each article, make your best decision, and write out the categories in front of JSON lines, for future reference. There should be two hierarchical tiers (area, topic), instead of three. You do not need to sort the JSON lines yet. Those JSON lines should still maintain their original ascending order according to their IDs. Compile all your results in a simple text file (step2.txt).

The step2.txt should contain something like this:

[Area 2: xxx / Topic 2.3: xxx] {"id": 33, "domain": "xxx", "title": "xxx"}
[Area 4: xxx / Topic 4.2: xxx] {"id": 34, "domain": "xxx", "title": "xxx"}
[Area 1: xxx / Topic 1.4: xxx] {"id": 35, "domain": "xxx", "title": "xxx"}

Let me make it clear again: These lines will be still ranked by their IDs in ascending order, just as they were first given in Step 1, **not** their area and topic orders yet. Because sorting according to area and topic is harder, we will do that sorting later.

# DAILY BRIEFING: APRIL 2025

## AREA 1: ECONOMIC POLICY & PERFORMANCE

### Tariffs and Trade War Impacts
The US economy has contracted in the first quarter of 2025, with multiple sources attributing this downturn to President Trump's tariff policies. Reuters reports that tariffs have "unleashed a flood of imports" [1], while economic reversal began in the run-up to tariff implementation [2]. Recession fears are mounting [3] and major employers are announcing layoffs, with UPS citing Trump's tariffs as it plans to cut 20,000 jobs [4]. On the international front, China has created a list of US-made goods exempt from its retaliatory 125% tariffs [5].

[1] US economy contracts in the first quarter; tariffs unleash flood of imports, https://www.reuters.com/business/stockpiling-ahead-tariffs-likely-hurt-us-economy-first-quarter-2025-04-30/  
[2] US economy went into reverse in run-up to Trump’s tariff shock, https://www.thetimes.com/business-money/companies/article/us-economy-went-into-reverse-in-run-up-to-trumps-tariff-shock-6tmlhnl79  
[3] The U.S. economy shrinks as Trump's tariffs spark recession fears, https://www.npr.org/2025/04/30/nx-s1-5380204/trump-economy-gdp-tariffs-recession-consumers  
[4] UPS cites Trump tariffs as it announces expected layoffs of 20,000 workers, https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2025/apr/30/ups-layoffs-trump-tariffs  
[5] China creates list of US-made goods exempt from 125% tariffs, sources say, https://www.reuters.com/world/china/china-creates-list-us-made-goods-exempt-125-tariffs-sources-say-2025-04-30/

  
### Economic Indicators and Administration Response
Economic indicators show private payroll growth slowed to just 62,000 in April, well below expectations [1]. The administration has attributed these declines to the previous administration, with President Trump blaming a Biden "overhang" for GDP contraction [2]. This represents a messaging shift, as Trump is now pinning stock market struggles on Biden just weeks after taking credit for market performance [3]. Trade adviser Peter Navarro has dismissed concerns about the GDP drop, stating "We really like where we're at now" [4].

[1] Private payroll growth slowed to 62,000 in April, well below expectations, https://www.cnbc.com/2025/04/30/adp-jobs-report-april-2025.html  
[2] Trump blames Biden 'overhang' after GDP shrinks in first quarter, says growth will 'take a while', https://www.cnbc.com/2025/04/30/trump-gdp-tariffs-biden-overhang.html  
[3] Trump pins stock market struggles on Biden — weeks after taking credit for it, https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/donald-trump/trump-pins-stock-market-struggles-biden-weeks-taking-credit-rcna203702?link_source=ta_bluesky_link&taid=68125a97925fde000100dba0&utm_campaign=trueanthem&utm_medium=social&utm_source=bluesky

## AREA 2: EXECUTIVE POWER & ADMINISTRATION

### Executive Orders and Power Expansion
President Trump's executive orders have significantly expanded presidential authority. The Atlantic reports an executive order implementing "Schedule F" will convert approximately 50,000 government employees into "de facto political appointees who serve only at the president’s pleasure" [1], representing a substantial restructuring of federal employment protections. The Nation characterizes Trump's newest executive order as one that "unleashes the cops—and flirts with martial law" [2], while The New Republic claims Republicans are moving to "expand Trump’s powers while no one is looking" [3].

### First 100 Days and DOGE Activities
The Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE), led by Elon Musk, faces ethical scrutiny as ProPublica reports "a DOGE aide involved in dismantling Consumer Bureau owns stock in companies that could benefit from the cuts" [1]. The President's first 100 days have generated mixed assessments, with reports examining Trump's "no ordinary cabinet" [2] and questions about potential conflicts of interest related to Trump's cryptocurrency firm [3]. Trump's communications remain contentious, with reports of him pressuring a journalist to accept a doctored photo as authentic [4] and lashing out against "fake polls" as approval ratings decline [5].

## AREA 3: IMMIGRATION ENFORCEMENT & BORDER POLICY

### Deportation Programs and the Abrego Garcia Case
President Trump's immigration enforcement has intensified, with efforts to "crack down on 'sanctuary cities'" [1] and arrangements "to deport Venezuelans to El Salvador’s most feared prison" [2]. The case of Kilmar Abrego Garcia has become a flashpoint, with Trump repeatedly stating he "could" return Abrego Garcia to the US but won't [3]. Controversy surrounds the evidence used for deportation, with reports Trump based the decision on an image that wasn't authentic [4]. El Salvador has reportedly "spurned U.S. request for return of the deported migrant" [5], while a judge has denied "DOJ's request to further delay discovery in Abrego Garcia case" [6].

### Impact on Communities and Judicial Intervention
Immigration enforcement actions are having profound effects on families and communities. The Independent reports "Trump’s deportations are turning immigrant communities into ghost towns" [1]. Individual cases have drawn criticism, including an incident where an "Oklahoma US citizen mother and daughters were terrorized by ICE agents in a botched search for immigrants" [2]. Meanwhile, courts are increasingly intervening, with judges ordering the release of both "a Palestinian man arrested at his US citizenship interview" [3] and "Columbia University student Mohsen Mahdawi detained by ICE" [4].

## AREA 4: CONGRESSIONAL & JUDICIAL OPPOSITION

### Democratic Strategy and Public Opinion
Congressional Democrats are formulating responses to the administration's agenda, with Time magazine assessing "What Congress Got Done in Trump’s First 100 Days" [1]. # DAILY BRIEFING: APRIL 2025

## AREA 1: ECONOMIC POLICY & PERFORMANCE

### Tariffs and Trade War Impacts
The US economy has contracted in the first quarter of 2025, with multiple sources attributing this downturn to President Trump's tariff policies. Reuters reports that tariffs have "unleashed a flood of imports" [1], while economic reversal began in the run-up to tariff implementation [2]. Recession fears are mounting [3] and major employers are announcing layoffs, with UPS citing Trump's tariffs as it plans to cut 20,000 jobs [4]. On the international front, China has created a list of US-made goods exempt from its retaliatory 125% tariffs [5].

[1] US economy contracts in the first quarter; tariffs unleash flood of imports, https://www.reuters.com/business/stockpiling-ahead-tariffs-likely-hurt-us-economy-first-quarter-2025-04-30/;

[4] UPS cites Trump tariffs as it announces expected layoffs of 20,000 workers, https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2025/apr/30/ups-layoffs-trump-tariffs;

### Economic Indicators and Administration Response
Economic indicators show private payroll growth slowed to just 62,000 in April, well below expectations [1]. The administration has attributed these declines to the previous administration, with President Trump blaming a Biden "overhang" for GDP contraction [2]. This represents a messaging shift, as Trump is now pinning stock market struggles on Biden just weeks after taking credit for market performance [3]. Trade adviser Peter Navarro has dismissed concerns about the GDP drop, stating "We really like where we're at now" [4].

[2] Trump blames Biden 'overhang' after GDP shrinks in first quarter, says growth will 'take a while', https://www.cnbc.com/2025/04/30/trump-gdp-tariffs-biden-overhang.html;  
[3] Trump pins stock market struggles on Biden — weeks after taking credit for it, https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/donald-trump/trump-pins-stock-market-struggles-biden-weeks-taking-credit-rcna203702?link_source=ta_bluesky_link&taid=68125a97925fde000100dba0&utm_campaign=trueanthem&utm_medium=social&utm_source=bluesky;

## AREA 2: EXECUTIVE POWER & ADMINISTRATION

### Executive Orders and Power Expansion
President Trump's executive orders have significantly expanded presidential authority. The Atlantic reports an executive order implementing "Schedule F" will convert approximately 50,000 government employees into "de facto political appointees who serve only at the president’s pleasure" [1], representing a substantial restructuring of federal employment protections. The Nation characterizes Trump's newest executive order as one that "unleashes the cops—and flirts with martial law" [2], while The New Republic claims Republicans are moving to "expand Trump’s powers while no one is looking" [3].

[1] DOGE Was Bad. Schedule F Will Be Worse. ### First 100 Days and DOGE Activities
The Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE), led by Elon Musk, faces ethical scrutiny as ProPublica reports "a DOGE aide involved in dismantling Consumer Bureau owns stock in companies that could benefit from the cuts" [1]. The President's first 100 days have generated mixed assessments, with reports examining Trump's "no ordinary cabinet" [2] and questions about potential conflicts of interest related to Trump's cryptocurrency firm [3]. Trump's communications remain contentious, with reports of him pressuring a journalist to accept a doctored photo as authentic [4] and lashing out against "fake polls" as approval ratings decline [5].

El Salvador has reportedly "spurned U.S. request for return of the deported migrant" [5], while a judge has denied "DOJ's request to further delay discovery in Abrego Garcia case" [6].

## 1. Economic Policy and Performance

### 1.1 Tariffs and Trade War Impacts
The US economy has contracted in the first quarter of 2025, with multiple sources attributing this downturn to President Trump's tariff policies. Reuters reports that tariffs have "unleashed a flood of imports" [1], while economic reversal began in the run-up to tariff implementation [2]. Recession fears are mounting [3] and major employers are announcing layoffs, with UPS citing Trump's tariffs as it plans to cut 20,000 jobs [4]. On the international front, China has created a list of US-made goods exempt from its retaliatory 125% tariffs [5].

Economic indicators show private payroll growth slowed to just 62,000 in April, well below expectations [1]. This represents a messaging shift, as Trump is now pinning stock market struggles on Biden just weeks after taking credit for market performance [3]. Trade adviser Peter Navarro has dismissed concerns about the GDP drop, stating "We really like where we're at now" [4].
